  17. I love, love, love this product. I love it so much that I'm writing a product review, which I never do, because I want to make sure enough people buy this so that it'll always be on the market for the times I need to replace the device. The one drawback I've found is that it must be handled with extreme care or else it will break, as mine did after six months of twice-weekly use, even though I never dropped it or otherwise manhandled it. If the makers could come out with a sturdier model, then it would be perfect. (When mine broke I returned to to the manufacturer--you'll need to include your receipt so make sure you hang onto it--and they sent me a brand new model within 3 weeks.) I have thick, coarse and naturally wavy hair. I have zero patience for blow drying and only have it blown dried and styled after my haircuts, after which I'm showered with compliments about my hair (which people will compare to Maria Shriver's, Dana Delany's or Cindy Crawfords). But when I let it air dry and don't style it, which is 70% of the time (I'm a mom), it just looks average like most women. With the Instyler I still put in minimal effort (still letting it air dry overnight), but now I get fabulous results after spending 15 minutes styling my hair in the morning with the device. And now the compliments flow more frequently. So the bottom line is that I get great looking hair with the most minimal effort, and that is worth the world to me since I'm a very low-maintenance person who still wants to look good. You'll get the same results if you blow dry your hair and then use less expensive straighteners and such, which for me would take at least an hour. To me it's worth investing in the InStyler to get the same results in a fraction of the time. Oh, and it takes a few tries to get it right, but once you do it's so easy to use. This is my first can't-live-without hair appliance ever.

  108. For those reviewers who said they couldn't use the InStyler because the barrel only rotates in one direction--you didn't figure out the secret. It doesn't matter which way it rotates. You just use the tool like a flat iron by slowly running it through your hair. The curl is created by the way you manage the styler, not by the way it rotates. If the barrel is placed underneath the hair, the hair curves under. If the barrel is placed on top of the hair, the hair flips out. You control the direction and tightness of the curl by the technique you use. I think if you want tight curls, you should use a curling iron. But this works great for waves and curves. I love my flat iron, but don't like the way it left my hair totally straight. I have naturally curly and frizzy hair and I love the InStyler for natural curves and no frizz!

  165. I have had my instyler about a year and I absolutely love it. It works beautifully for my thick relatively fine shoulder length hair. My hair has a lot of wave and can look 'fuzzy'. There are a couple of keys to using it - I read a lot of the other negative reviews - and here is my advise:<br />1. Use a defrizz product to go with it - I love John Frieda \\"Frizz Ease\\" wherer I take a dollop about the size of a quarter - rub in on my hands and between my fingers and run them through my hair.<br />2. Brush your hair well to get the product nicely distributed.<br />3. Don't take too much hair! I gather up about the top 80% of my hair into a clip or pony tail and start with the hair underneath. Then I take about a fourth of that hair - start at the scalp and smooth down - holding the ends a little longer if I want them to flip.<br />4. Finish that layer - brush.<br />5. Let hair down - release about another 20 percent and repeat with that layer.<br />6. Continue through all the layers.<br /><br />Now, this sounds like a lot of work - it takes me about 15 minutes on the morning after a hairwash. The next day - its a 5 minute touchup.<br /><br />So - my advice - don't take too much hair, start from the most underneath hair and work up. And be careful - it is HOT!

  205. I have been using the InStyler for 2 weeks. I have below shoulder length thick course wavy hair. I kept all the packaging and the receipt so that I could return it if it didn't work out. After getting used to it, I have decided to keep it. CONS: 1 - The barrel only rotates one way. When I used it the first time, my hair looked frizzy and terrible, but I figured out that the barrel was rotating upwards and I was pulling it downwards. After I figured out that the barrel should be rotating in the direction that I was pulling it, then it worked fine. My guess is that people who don't like this iron are probably holding the iron incorrectly. It is very awkward always holding the iron in a way so that the barrel is rolling in the right direction. When I use a regular flatiron, I hold it in my right hand and pull it through the left side of my head, and then hold it in my left hand and pull it through the right side of my head. You cannot do that with this iron. I have to hold it with the handle pointing to the back of my head which is really really awkward. 2 - It doesn't curl my hair very well, but that's not a deal breaker for me. If I want to curl my hair, I just use a regular iron, but I don't curl my hair very often. 3 - You need to use very small sections of hair. I am used to using larger sections with my regular flat iron. 4 - It doesn't work on my bangs. If you have short hair, I don't recommend this iron. 5 - It doesn't work on damp hair AT ALL. It is much easier to have your hair completely dry. PROS: 1 - Once you get used to holding it correctly and using smaller sections of hair, it does work very well. I can make my hair straight, curled under or flip up, and it has great body. 2 - The style lasts until I wash it. I only wash my hair every three days, and I only have to touch up my hair slightly each day with the InStyler. 3 - My hair feels silky and shiny. My old flat iron doesn't do that. BUT I do use a hair serum (Olive Oil brand) even though the directions says not to have any product in your hair (I've always used the serum, even with other tools). My hair does not look as smooth and silky without the serum. 4 - My ultimate test was this morning. I washed my hair last night and let it air dry (my hair has a weird wave). I woke up to a hot mess. But the InStyler had no problem smoothing my hair out perfectly. To keep my hair healthy, I will probably always wash at night, let it air dry, and then straighten it in the morning. All in all, I recommend this for people with long hair who want to straighten or flip their hair.

  240. I am currently on my second InStyler. The first, my husband got me for Christmas 2 years ago and I fell in love! I am completely a hair style failure - using any kind of styling tool just ends up making my hair look worse than it did before. But the InStyler made everything super simple. I've read some people complaining about not being able to use both hands while styling because there's not a cool place to hold on the end. I can see why this is a problem for other irons but you honestly do not need 2 hands for this. If you hold the InStyler closed tight and firm and pull down the length of the hair slow, it works perfectly. I think more of these \\"complaints\\" are user error. But there are some downfalls. Cons: - It can be awkward to get used to, especially after learning that you have to hold it so that it rotates with your hair instead of against it. If you hold the rotating barrel on the under side of your hair, you'll end up with little fly-aways. It's nothing a little hairspray at the end can't handle but still a disappointment. Holding the rotating barrel on the top side of your hair gets rid of those fly-aways but it's really awkward to style that. Or at least it is for me. I just hold it how it's comfortable and deal with the fly-aways at the end with hairspray or a quick sweep with a regular straightener. - The InStyler get EXTREMELY hot. To me, this is a plus. Every salon I have been tells me I have the thickest hair they have ever seen. It's a huge pain and has a mind of it's own. So I always use the highest heat setting and it styles my hair instantly. I can see how this would be a downfall for others with thinner hair as the intense heat does make the styling process a bit more cautionary. - The bristles. Ah, those damn bristles! The bristles are why I am on my second InStyler. My first is still running like a champ but the bristles on the brush end look like a 30 year old abused broom - they're all frayed and pushedapart. They were barely even brushing my hair as I was straightening anymore so I had to get a second one. Unfortunately, the second one is starting to show a bit of use as well in the bristles but I'm hanging in there. For as expensive as this tool is, I would think they would sell replacement parts, such as the bristles, that you can easily slide in and out when needed. This is definitely something they should consider. I was none too happy when I had to buy another entire unit just because the bristles were pooped out. - It seems the InStyler was originally designed for professional hair stylists and just got passed to us common folk. When I use it on other people's hair, their hair looks beautiful - just like it does on the models in the commercial. And I think \\"Now why can't I get MINE to look like that?!\\" And it's all because that's what it was originally made for, I believe. Not a deal breaker but they should've redesigned it to make it less awkward and more user-friendly for people doing their own hair. Pros - When I would use regular straighteners before, it would take me at least an hour to get my whole head done and to be sure there weren't any pieces left unstraightened. It even takes my hair stylist a good 45 minutes to get my hair completely straight. With the InStyler, it takes me 20 minutes, tops. - As I said, my super thick hair with a wave straight from the Pacific Coast, I didn't have my sights set too high for this thing. The test was when I went to bed with my hair wet the night before and woke up to looking like a wild bush woman. The InStyler had no problem getting it back to a tamed, manageable place. Granted, sometimes, I may have to go over the same piece 2 or 3 times but who doesn't do that anyway? - Anything that wasn't a con, is a pro. I just love this thing. I do use a regular hair straightener after I'm done with the InStyler but it's not necessary. This thing is a beast and an answer to my hair-prayers!

I will admit that it did take awhile to receive my order since the company is in Canada but that's nothing either the company or I could help. I received both Instylers, 2 combs, 2 travel bags, 2 training protectors, a heat protective counter mat, and an instructional DVD. The main reason I purchased this product is because having thin hair I have never gotten my hair to hold any kind of curl. My hair is naturally wavy but I must put a lot of product in it to get it to even hold what little curl it has. I washed my hair with shampoo and conditioner and then blow-dried as I normally would. I then sectioned my hair and began the curling process. Yes the styler will get hot, it will be very hot. As almost every styling tool does. The Instyler does have 3 heat settings and the finer your hair the less heat you probably need. That being said I did use mine on the highest setting. And yes, I did burn myself. I just feel that it comes with the territory of using a heated styling tool. In fact, I've burnt myself without just about every curling iron and straightener I've ever owned. To curl your hair you simply wrap sections of your hair around the tool, squeeze the tool together allowing the iron to rotate for a few seconds, release and allow your hair to gently fall away from the iron. My hair had a perfect curl! Better results than I've ever gotten in my entire life. The tool does make a noise when the barrel is rotating, it doesn't bother me because if it has moving parts I expect it to make noise. I was ableto curl my entire head of hair in about 30 minutes. Yes there is a learning curve because the Instyler should be held a certain way to get the results your are looking for, but it took me a few days getting used to my straightener so I think a couple of uses and a little patience is all you need. Those of you who may be worried about heat damage, that happens any time you use heat on your hair. You should be conditioning your hair and using some of kind of heat protectant no matter what styling tool your are using. Plus give it more than one shot, nothing is perfect the first time you do it.

I run it down the section of hair a couple of times to smooth it and then I just let it sit for about 6 seconds on the ends and it puts a nice curl on the ends. It also works really well if I want to put long curls in. I just wrap it like a curling iron and hold it in place for 5-7 seconds. It takes me about 25 minutes to do my hair. I can see how it may not work as well on thick, very curly hair, but on my hair type it works great. I have never had any mechanical issues with either of the Instylers. It is a little noisy but you get used to that...but don't expect to listen to the television while you are using it.

With those options, you would have a better functioning straightening iron. I don't recommend this if you need to use it as a curling iron, however, because then the rotating barrel has nothing to hold the curl in place. Increased to two stars.
